## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and concentration A, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. The rate law typically depends on powers of concentration, and time dependence may arise from external forcing or complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface catalysis kinetics)
- Time-dependent decay with reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated rate)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate with source/sink)
- Competitive inhibition form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Sigmoidal kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding kinetics)
- Damped time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (linearly time-varying rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate constants in dA/dt indicate consumption of reactant A; positive constants indicate production or reversibility
- Integer power-law exponents on concentration correspond to elementary reaction molecularity (1=unimolecular, 2=bimolecular, 3=trimolecular)
- Rational functions of concentration (A/(c+A)) indicate saturation mechanisms such as enzyme catalysis or surface adsorption
- Products of concentration with (c-A) terms suggest autocatalytic or logistic-type mechanisms with a carrying capacity
- Polynomial combinations of different powers of A suggest parallel competing reaction pathways
- Explicit time dependence in rate expressions suggests external forcing (light, temperature ramp) or non-autonomous kinetic systems
- Square root dependence on A (A**0.5) can arise from chain reaction mechanisms with radical intermediates
- Rate expressions with A appearing in both numerator and denominator suggest pre-equilibrium or quasi-steady-state approximation mechanisms
